< review>
One Saturday afternoon on a long weekend, I was "Yelping" ( I guess that is a term these days for searching:-)) for an Optometrist with 5 star reviews, open till late, in the Tri-Valley, and accepts VSP! Hurray!! I found Imagine Optometry!!! Thrilled and excited, I decided to drive there. The office ambience is very contemporary and I really liked the colorful paintings of Gandhi and the Beatles! Staff was super friendly! I was able to schedule my whole family's appointment for the next day which was a Sunday!  Fast forward to the appointment next day, All of us were very impressed with Dr. Truong. He is super knowledgeable and extremely patient and helpful! The exam was very thorough! Now it was time to select the glasses:-).  Which can be fun but challenging too! Margaret, the receptionist, was great in helping us pick the right front frames. But a HUGE loud Shout-out Mary, Dr. Truong's wife! She is awesome! Mary is extremely patient, helpiful, and knowledgeable! She helped each of us pick frames, took care of the measurements and all the paperwork! My teenage son had hard time selecting the frame. The staff was super friendly and helpful. They were not at all pushy and didn't try to promote expensive frames and add ons!  My son ended up picking frame from Imagine line. ( that's when we found that the talented and creative couple also has their designer frame line.)

Dr Truong was very helpful and knowledgeable in that he mentioned getting work glasses with anti-reflective coating would help block blue light that emits from digital devices. <gmap_id>0x808fe8d9baaaa84b:0xd081abffa29246bc<//gmap_id>< Text>
I usually do not write reviews for businesses but I had to for this place. I found Imagine Optometry via the VSP website. I went with them purely based on the fact that they had the most fresh, well designed, and interesting website.

Note to all you other optometrists in the Bay Area, spend some money and update your websites!! They look like they were designed in the early 2000. We live in a time that responsive design is a must. As a person that works in the tech industry I will always close your website and move on within seconds of seeing how your website is designed. First impressions are a must.

Anyways, Imagine Optometry‚Äôs online appointment process was super easy and fast. I was able to get an appointment in minutes and received text message updates that made things very convenient.

My appointment experience was amazing. The facility was super cool and hype. Beautiful displays and the best artwork on the walls.

Dr. Truong was really nice and knowledgeable. He told me things about my eyes that no other optometrist has ever told me. I have been seeing different optometrist for 36 years now and I wonder why they felt like that info was not important to tell me.

Coolest thing of all was that within minutes I realized where the name Imagine came from. This place was inspired by John Lennon and you can see it all over the place. As a music lover and musician I appreciated that so much. Dr. Truong was also very knowledgeable in music so our conversation was awesome. We talked music the whole time which I loved.

The only downside of Imagine Optometry is that it‚Äôs new and so Dr Truong does not have the assistance of others. He was kind of a one man shop but that didn‚Äôt change my rating which is still 5 stars.

I will be a long time patient for sure!! This place is amazing.</Text>

< Text>
(Translated by Google) A view of the Long Valley Caldera from the past volcanic eruptions and the later Crawley Lake.

Crawley Lake, which appears to be caldera, is said to have erupted past volcanic ash from more than 1,000 miles to Texas. Imagine a tremendous amount of ash covering the sky and no sunlight, so there is no disaster.

It is a place where you can feel the freshness of the long trip with the cool breeze and the panoramic view. It's also a good idea to stretch and look out at the view and even sign up.

< Text>
(Translated by Google) This lake next to the road can be seen thanks to a Parador located right next to it.
This lake of volcanic origin was formed due to a large explosion thousands of years ago. Despite being located next to the Sierra Nevada mountain range, there is a difference of about 2000 meters from the highest point to the lake. The water of this and other lakes in the area is used by the neighboring villages and by the cattle of the calf farms so typical of this territory.

Waste of time. The lender advertises unsecured loans to help establish credit within the Hispanic community - specifically targetting immigrants and those with no or low credit. Then you will go through a lengthy documentation process where they will bother personal references which is fine, but then when the loan offer comes in it will be substantially less credit than you anticipated. Because of their lengthy process and the hassle to any of your references, it's easier in most cases to build credit with a low limit credit card.< /Review>

< review>
Great museum with a twist. It's one of the only museums I've been to that encourages you to touch, open, and sit in just about any of the cars in their collection!  Awesome selection of cars from the early 1900s up through the late 80s or early 90s, domestic and foreign. Did the whole thing in under 2 hours and that was reading about most of the cars. Great way to kill a couple hours near LAX. Highly recommend!</review>

< Text>
What a treasure! If you can go on a Sunday afternoon, be sure and make a reservation to take a ride in one of their historic cars. Each week they choose three different classic automobiles and will give rides. Otherwise  there is an excellent display of a variety of classic cars and usually a volunteer or two who will show you around and answer any questions. The gift shop is well priced and has some nice souvenirs. And there's actually in ice cream shop which makes a delightful stop even if you aren't interested in automobiles.</Text>

<Time>1528850275153< /Time><Rating>4< /Rating>< review>
Solid collection of American vintage cars. Some are more esoteric than they are culturally significant, so keep that in mind.

They're all crammed in a single room, which might make appreciating some of them difficult-- hard to take in the beauty with another car three feet away on two sides.

I waver on 3* or 4*, but I'm feeling generous... and the location is great-- perfect for a quick visit from LAX if you have a few hours' layover, but not enough time to venture all the way to the Petersen!</review>

<Text>Went to meet up with friends from Riverside & Pasadena. Our Pasadena friends couldn't make it! Yet we still enjoyed the museum.

Their was a car show today. Muscle cars from the 60's, 70's, 80's & a very few newer model hi performance cars. Now, this is not a large show. Take away the museums cars & maybe there was 35 cars. So unless your a big car fan, probably not for you.

All the cars were terrific & the owners prides showed through.

One nice component of the museum, if it's the museums car, you can get, sit down & check it out.

For me it was coming all of 15 minutes from Redondo, so no issues. My friends from 80 miles away, we're a little disappointed, understandably so. But they still enjoyed their day.

If your local, go. If your coming from 30 miles plus, i'd wait till they have a large show.<//Text>< name>

<Name>Chris Fortunato</Name>< userid>
112226215222316010023< /userid>
<gmap_id>0x80c2b6b4c634ce57:0xba0f46475dfe3e29<//gmap_id><Date>1500241680092<//Date>< review>
I'm a long-time car guy, and while this place has some interesting vehicles, it's not nearly as diverse as one might expect, and unfortunately it has no flow. One big room, with a second that requires a chaperone (docent), with cars packed in haphazardly. There is very little history or much of any real information on the cars themselves (mostly because they are drivers, and they allow you to gently crawl around in them), which would help the experience. It is a non-profit, and admission is suggested donations, but I would have liked to see a little more than a garage full of cars. Still, for what it is, I'm really glad it's there, we need more of this.< /review>

<Rate>5< /Rate>< Text>
Very interesting, not overwhelming.  Docents all over to help you with any questions.  Very nice staff.  Went on a Sunday which is when they take cars out, so we took three different car rides (free).  They ask an entry donation as they are a non-profit of $10 each for adults.  Well worth every penny to help keep the cars running.  All the cars there registered and are for "driving".  They even allow you to get in the cars on the museum floor.  If you've ever wondered how it feels to climb into the driver's seat of a Delorean, they have one in the collection.<//Text>

< text>
The Automobile Driving Museum has its name referring to the very interesting fact that all the cars in the museum are ready to drive on the street. This is quite a challenge to keep all these machines ready for use on the street, Really Amazing. Another point of interest is the note that the museum's admission charge is a recommended donation.  Note only recommended. The autos are in one large room with about eighty cars. There is a glassed in room that visitors are not allowed to enter that houses the ultra rare classics that can be viewed from a distance. There are cars here that are in the Rose Parade each year, cars that  have carried dignitaries and even one customized Packard Pickup conversion. I found the quality quantity and condition of all the cars to be excellent. After talking to one of the docents I learned that they had several cars on loan from the Peterson Museum. Quite an honor to have loaners from such a prestigious museum. The Automobile Driving Museum also has multiple additional warehouses with several hundred other cars that they rotate into the displays. This makes the museum ever changing and always interesting. Each Sunday they choose three cars and give people rides in the cars. Every Sunday they choose three different cars. Wow! and if you check in with Yelp there is an offer for Free Ice Creams. What a deal! The quality and selection of autos is marvelous and it is a worthy stop for anyone. When I was picking up my son who came in on a flight at Los Angeles International Airport, it was a simple 5 minute drive to pick him up. I found the museum to be a much more satisfying stop than a cell phone parking lot at the airport. So, plan a little extra time into your airport pickup or drop off and enjoy The Automobile Driving Museum. It is another one of the many small museums in beautiful Los Angeles area.<//text>
